        <p class="date">
         Sat Jan 19, 2013 at 04:30 AM PST
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2013/01/19/1180214/-Abbreviated-Pundit-Round-up-Questions-and-answers-and-more-questions" id="titleHref">
          Abbreviated Pundit Round-up: Questions and answers and more questions
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/Greg Dworkin">
          Greg Dworkin
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=426&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
         <span class="for">
          for
         </span>
         <a href="/blog/main">
          Daily Kos
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2013/01/19/1180214/-Abbreviated-Pundit-Round-up-Questions-and-answers-and-more-questions" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="Abbreviated Pundit Round-up: Questions and answers and more questions" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2013/01/19/1180214/-Abbreviated-Pundit-Round-up-Questions-and-answers-and-more-questions" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="206" data-story_id="1180214" href="/story/2013/01/19/1180214/-Abbreviated-Pundit-Round-up-Questions-and-answers-and-more-questions#comments">
           206 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <div class="dkimg-c">
          <span class="image_container">
           <img alt="chart of 5 polls post newtown on stricter gun laws" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/dk-production/images/16001/large/gunpolls.jpg?1358515841"/>
          </span>
          <div class="dkimg-cap">
           Data compiled from
           <a href="http://www.pollingreport.com/guns.htm">
            pollingreport.com
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <br/>
         <p>
          <a href="http://thehill.com/opinion/columnists/juan-williams/277893-gun-action-central-to-obamas-presidency">
           The Hill
          </a>
          :
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          But a new political reality dawned after the Newtown shooting.
          <p>
           The president was bluntly asked in a White House news conference: Whereve you been? on gun control. He responded curtly that the shooting had been a wake-up call.
          </p>
          <p>
           And before any Inaugural balls, the president appeared at the White House with schoolchildren who implored him to do something about gun violence.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <a href="http://www.gallup.com/poll/159959/americans-reaction-obama-gun-proposals-positive.aspx">
          Gallup
         </a>
         :
         <blockquote>
          Americans' immediate reaction to President Barack Obama's proposals for new laws designed to reduce gun violence is more positive than negative, with 53% saying they would want their representative in Congress to vote for the set of proposed new laws, while 41% say their representative should vote against them.
         </blockquote>
         The only sub-groups that oppose it are conservatives and Republicans. Duh. Hugely popular in the East (68-30), marginally popular out West (47-45). Midwest (50-42) and South (49-44) okay with it.
         <p>
          <a href="http://nymag.com/daily/intelligencer/2013/01/david-brooks-now-totally-pathological.html">
           Jonathan Chait
          </a>
          on David Brooks:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          Moderate Republicanism is a tendency that increasingly defies ideological analysis and instead requires psychological analysis. The psychological mechanism is fairly obvious. The radicalization of the GOP has placed unbearable strain on those few moderates torn between their positions and their attachment to party. Many moderate conservatives have simply broken off from the party, at least in its current incarnation, and are hoping or working to build a sane alternative. Those who remain must escape into progressively more baroque fantasies.
         </blockquote>
         <a href="http://www.sacbee.com/2013/01/17/5120165/whether-or-not-torture-works-theres.html">
          Leonard Pitts Jr
         </a>
         :
         <blockquote>
          Does torture work? Beg pardon, but we have been asking the wrong question. What matters is not whether torture works. What matters is whether torture is right.
          <p>
           Consider: Mothers Against Drunk Driving reports that drunk drivers kill almost 10,000 people a year. That's three Sept. 11's and then some. But if you wanted to stop that carnage, it would be simple. Just make drunk driving a capital crime with instant punishment. The evidence  blood alcohol levels  allows for scientific certainty of guilt, so there'd be no need of a long trial. We could execute the miscreants within a day.
          </p>
          <p>
           Drunk driving would disappear. The new policy would solve the problem. It would work.
          </p>
          <p>
           And if that were truly the ultimate rubric by which we decided a question, there could be no argument against it. But we won't make drunk driving a capital crime for one simple reason.
          </p>
          <p>
           It would be wrong. In fact, it would be repellent to our values, inconsonant with the kind of people we consider ourselves to be.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <a href="http://dallasmorningviewsblog.dallasnews.com/2013/01/lance-armstrong-meet-manti-teo-and-indifference.html/">
          Sharon Grigsby
         </a>
         /Dallas Morning News:
         <blockquote>
          Even before the Teo story broke, some were already saying enough already about Armstrong. I particularly liked
          <a href="http://www.dallasnews.com/opinion/latest-columns/20130116-melinda-henneberger-enough-already-with-the-apology-tour-mr.-livestrong.ece">
           this one
          </a>
          from Washington Post writer Melinda Henneberger, which we published on Viewpoints today. Perhaps Ive just seen one too many replays of Armstrongs steadfast (and at times angry, in-your-face) denials, which have looped endlessly this week on the news channels. As this former fan, who believed those denials for far too long, I think Armstrong is getting his just deserts for his years of cheating and bullying: growing indifference.
         </blockquote>
         <a href="http://www.pcmag.com/article2/0,2817,2414456,00.asp">
          PCMag.com
         </a>
         :
         <blockquote>
          Opponents of the new NRA shooting app for iOS are calling on Apple to pull it from the App Store because its release is insensitive so soon after the Newtown shooting.
          <p>
           "The National Rifle Association's new app 'NRA: Practice Range' is an insult to the victims of gun violence, having been launched on the one month anniversary of the Sandy Hook shooting," according to the petition posted on Signon.org. "Out of respect for the victims and to signal Apple's support for common sense measures to help end gun violence, we call on you to rescind your approval of this shameless new product."
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <a href="http://www.foxnews.com/politics/2013/01/18/fox-news-poll-twice-as-many-favor-more-guns-over-banning-guns-to-reduce-violent/">
          Fox News
         </a>
         leads with "America loves guns" and "nothing will change", but here's what their own poll actually shows:
         <blockquote>
          On Wednesday President Obama announced several gun-control proposals. Among them: requiring background checks for all gun buyers and banning military-style assault weapons and high-capacity magazines.
          <p>
           The poll asked about these as well as other possible ways to reduce gun violence. (A portion of the interviews were conducted before Obamas formal announcement.)
          </p>
          <p>
           The most popular suggestions are requiring criminal background checks on all gun buyers (with 91 percent favoring this proposal), providing services for mentally ill people who show violent tendencies (89 percent) and improving enforcement of existing laws (86 percent)
          </p>
          <p>
           Large majorities also favor mandating mental-health checks on gun buyers (83 percent) and requiring criminal background checks on anyone buying ammunition (80 percent).
           <br/>
           Smaller majorities favor putting armed guards in schools (60 percent), banning high-capacity clips (56 percent), banning assault weapons (54 percent), and reducing access to violent movies and video games (52 percent).
          </p>
          <p>
           The least popular suggestion tested -- and the only one a majority opposes -- is allowing teachers and school officials to carry guns on school grounds (42 percent favor, 52 percent oppose).
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <a href="http://www.latimes.com/health/la-me-flu-vaccine-20130119,0,7186913.story">
          LA Times
         </a>
         :
         <blockquote>
          As flu cases increase, hospital administrators are grappling with whether to compel doctors, nurses and other medical staff to get vaccinated. Each year, only about 60% of hospital workers get the shot, according to a report by the California Department of Public Health. The federal government has set a goal of 90% by 2020.
         </blockquote>
         In general, medical societies and hospital associations support mandatory vaccine, nursing unions support the shot and recommend it but oppose the mandate. People don't like mandates. But mandates are what makes things work. Then again, so does honoring collective bargaining and working it out via negotiation. On the third hand, as my friend David Waldman is apt to note, freedom, liberty and Hitler (and no, it's not rational, so don't try and make sense of it. Then again, opposition to flu shots isn't rational, either.)
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
        </div>
       </div>

        <br/>
        <div>
         <p>
          Add keywords that describe this diary.
		Separate multiple keywords with commas.
          <br/>
          <a href="/special/tag_tips" target="_blank">
           Tagging tips
          </a>
          -
          <a href="/search?search_tags=1" target="_blank">
           Search For Tags
          </a>
          -
          <a href="http://www.dkosopedia.com/wiki/Tag:Tagfinder" target="_blank">
           Browse For Tags
          </a>
         </p>
         <div class="pageTip hasTooltip" style="margin-top:3px">
          ?
         </div>
         <div class="tooltipContents qtip-style-dk4_large qtip-pos-br">
          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>
         </div>
         <!-- &lt;h4 id="p_tagErrorMessage"&gt;You must enter at least one Tag for this Diary Entry:&lt;/h4&gt; -->
         <p>
          <input id="p_tagInput" name="tag_draft" size="70" type="text" value=""/>
          <!-- &lt;input id="tagSubmit" type="submit" name="submit" value="Submit" /&gt; -->
         </p>
         <p style="font-style:italic">
          Consider if one or more of these tags fits your diary:
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Civil Rights');return false;">
           Civil Rights
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Community');return false;">
           Community
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Congress');return false;">
           Congress
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Culture');return false;">
           Culture
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Economy');return false;">
           Economy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Education');return false;">
           Education
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Elections');return false;">
           Elections
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Energy');return false;">
           Energy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Environment');return false;">
           Environment
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Health Care');return false;">
           Health Care
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('International');return false;">
           International
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Labor');return false;">
           Labor
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Law');return false;">
           Law
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Media');return false;">
           Media
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Meta');return false;">
           Meta
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('National Security');return false;">
           National Security
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Science');return false;">
           Science
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Transportation');return false;">
           Transportation
          </a>
          , or
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('White House');return false;">
           White House
          </a>
          .
	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('California');return false;">
           California
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Texas');return false;">
           Texas
          </a>
          , etc).
	Keep in mind, though, that there are many wonderful and important diaries
	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.
         </p>

              from Mother Jones with Mackie- he calls himself a "liberal Libertarian", but he does have some liberal views:
             </p>
             <blockquote>
              I reject the premise that liberal and libertarian values are necessarily in conflict. In fact, I often self-identify as a "classical liberal." I am pro-choice, favor legalizing gay marriages, protecting our environment, enforcing strict animal welfare protection laws (I've been an ethical vegan for 10 years), marijuana legalization, having a welfare safety net for our poorest or disabled citizens, and a radically reduced defense budget and military presence around the world. However, I'm also a conscious capitalistI believe economic freedom and entrepreneurship are the best ways to end poverty, increase prosperity, and evolve humanity upward. I believe that all forms of socialism have been proven over time to result in a loss of both economic and civil liberties, with increasing poverty. The truth is that I don't fit into a simple ideological box. I read widely on issues, try to think carefully about them, and then I make up my own mind.
             </blockquote>
             But he's also a bit of that RWNJ Libertarian:
             <blockquote>
              The deficit problems can be completely explained by too much governmental spending. Spending at all levels has significantly increased in the past 12 years under both presidents, Bush and Obama. We could bring the annual federal budget into the black within just 10 years by simply limiting increases in spending to 2 percent per year. No additional taxes are required and I believe taxes are already too high in the United States. For example, our corporate income taxes are already the highest in the world.
             </blockquote>
             <a href="http://www.motherjones.com/environment/2013/01/whole-foods-market-john-mackey-interview-conscious-capitalism?page=1">
              http://www.motherjones.com/...
             </a>

              Not sure what to think!

             </div>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               Mackie is obviously pragmatic about social issues, but does not understand economic issues. When he remarks that spending at all levels has increased significantly under both Bush and Obama, he doesn't stop to ask "spending on what" and "why"? There is a huge difference between spending on necessities (keeping unemployed and underpaid people from suffering) and spending on wants (waging wars) and desires (further enriching the already rich).
              </p>
              <p>
               Most Libertarians want smaller government and fewer regulations on businesses regardless of what government is tasked to do. President Obama has reduced the size of government, unlike President Bush who massively increased the size and reach of government. The number of government employees has fallen dramatically under the current president; under the previous president the number of government employees increased dramatically. President Bush significantly reduced regulation on businesses, which turned out to be a threat to health, safety and the environment not to mention what it did to the world economy.
              </p>
              <p>
               Furthermore the "deficit problems" can not be "completely explained by too much government spending." If there are deficit problems - which is questionable - they are more a result of unemployment and underemployment than too much spending.
              </p>
              <p>
               Mackie needs to spend more time studying up on macroeconomics and less on rationalizing his current economic ideology.
              </p>
             </div>

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               is weird.
               <br/>
              </p>
              <blockquote>
               all forms of socialism have been proven over time to result in a loss of both economic and civil liberties, with increasing poverty.
              </blockquote>
              Exactly what does he mean by "all forms"? Certainly the socialism Marx would've like to see has never been tried. After the countries that had socialist revolutions, either the revolutionaries took power "until the working class was educated enough to run things" (and then they never ceded power, of course), or allied capitalist countries hit them with embargoes, sanctions, isolation, etc. in order to stifle any success that economy might have . . . or both. Or we just go assassinate the leaders and overthrow the fledgling governments (Iran, Chile, Grenada, Nicaragua, etc.). So we really haven't seen "all forms of socialism" really given a opportunity.
              <p>
               And the Democratic Socialism of Europe, though economically based in Capitalism, has done more for their citizens than our country's safety net has.
              </p>

                  I think there's a level of capitalism there, but it has to be regulated. The people on the top can't rig the system so that they receive massive government welfare in addition to their "profits".

            <p class="sig">
             "Politics is the art of looking for trouble, finding it everywhere, diagnosing it incorrectly and applying the wrong remedies." - Groucho Marx
            </p>
            <p class="cb">
             by
             <a href="/user/uid:426">
              Greg Dworkin
             </a>
             on
             <a href="/comments/1180214/49120929#c19">
              Sat Jan 19, 2013 at 05:11:50 AM PST
             </a>
            </p>
            <p class="cl">
             [
             <a href="#c4">
              Parent
             </a>
             ]
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>
         <ul class="cm i1" id="k49120929">
          <li id="c127">
           <div class="cx" id="cx49121443">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              "David Brooks Now Totally Pathological"
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1180214/49121443#c127?mode=alone;showrate=1#c127">
               2+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:66091">
                snazzzybird
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:5137">
                glitterscale
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              is the proper title for the piece.
              <br/>
             </p>
             <blockquote>
              Moderate Republicanism... requires psychological analysis. ...Moderate conservatives... must escape into progressively more baroque fantasies.
             </blockquote>
             The
             <strong>
              John Birch Society wing of the GOP
             </strong>
             got itself retagged as a "tea party" in 2009. That camouflage allowed it to take another 38 seats from Business Republicans in the 2010 elections.
             <p>
              Birchers now hold 150 seats in the House, versus 84 seats to the Business GOPers.
              <br/>
             </p>
             <blockquote>
              The prevalent expression of (Bizzie GOPer) psychological pain is the belief that President Obama is largely or entirely responsible for Republican extremism. Its a bizarre but understandable way to reconcile conflicting emotions.... In this case, moderate Republicans believe that Obamas tactic of taking sensible positions that moderate Republicans agree with is cruel and unfair, because it exposes the extremism that dominates the party, not to mention the powerlessness of the moderates within it.
             </blockquote>
             The 800-pound gorilla in GOPer politics is that the goddamn Birch Society and the billionaires who finance their wack-job projects now have enough of their candidates elected/in office to dominate the Republican Party.
             <p>
              Birchers started rolling up Bizzie congressional seats in 1984. This went on steadily for Safe seats through 2004. Then they made their latest giant step in 2010.
             </p>
             <p>
              You see Bircher Madness spew from the mouths of congressional Birchers every week. Here's a sample of Bircher Madness topics off today's jbs.org web site:
              <br/>
             </p>
             <blockquote>
              -- Government Attitude Towards Elderly Leads to Euthanasia
              <br/>
              -- Oppose Ratification of the UN Treaty on Disability Rights
              <br/>
              -- Voter Fraud
              <br/>
              -- Signs of a Declining Economy
              <br/>
              -- Russia Rising
              <br/>
              -- Communism Isn't Dead
              <br/>
              -- Nobel Prize Goes to EU. Communist President of EU Commission Thankful.
              <br/>
              -- Arab Unrest and Voter Fraud (in America somehow)
              <br/>
              -- Ron Paul Drummed Out of Republican Party
              <br/>
              -- Questions about the Aurora Colorado Movie Shooting
              <br/>
              -- Attack on Christianity and Restore Religious Freedom in America
              <br/>
              -- United Nations Ordering U.S. Troops to War
              <br/>
              -- Long-term Goal of a United Nations Standing Army Behind the Syria Solution
             </blockquote>
             That's normal stuff in the House. The Birch Society 2013 also considers "Corruption of the Republican Party" to be helping to govern the country along with democrats. I.e., normal politics.
             <p>
              Helluva 800-pound gorilla. The most of them gorillas don't have billionaires paying their bills! This one got sugar daddies by the dozen.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="cf">
             <p class="sig">
              "We have done nothing to be ashamed of. We have nothing to apologize for." NRA 12/14/2012 "Have you left no sense of decency, sir, at long last?" Army/McCarthy 1954
             </p>

           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Ron Fournier
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1180214/49121073#c71?mode=alone;showrate=1#c71">
              4+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:158085">
               commonmass
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:105891">
               JML9999
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:166705">
               tb mare
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:66091">
               snazzzybird
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             has been writing about the "chip" on Obama's shoulder, and then he wrote this yesterday:
             <br/>
             <a href="http://www.nationaljournal.com/politics/obama-s-inaugural-with-malice-or-none-20130118">
              Obama's Inaugural: With Malice or None?
             </a>
             <br/>
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             <strong>
              It would be natural for Barack Obama to begin his second term with a chip on his shoulder, emboldened by a reelection victory
             </strong>
             that, viewed through his eyes, ratified his agenda and punished his rivals for extremism. It also would be a mistake.
             <br/>
             Starting with his inaugural address on Monday, the president might want to consider the example of another former Illinois lawmaker who rose from obscurity to assume the presidency at a time of peril. Like President Obama, Abraham Lincoln had to triangulate between harsh obstructionists from an opposing party and radicals from within his own. Lincoln won reelection and faced the heady task of Reconstruction.
             <br/>
             While Lincolns times and tests were more challenging than those of today, his second inaugural address is a model for its modesty.
             <strong>
              Lincolns overall tone was humble, wrote historian Evan Thomas for The Daily Beast, that of a man who has learned from harsh experience.
             </strong>
             
            </blockquote>
            Obama is not going to come out swinging at Congress in his inaugural address, or at Republicans. Anyone who thinks otherwise is an idiot and hasn't been paying attention these last 4 years.
           </div>

                 at the risk of being a know it all

                <dl>
                 <dt>
                  Recommended by:

                 <dd>
                  <a href="/user/uid:49657">
                   HudsonValleyMark
                  </a>
                 </dd>
                </dl>
               </div>
               <div class="ct">
                <p>
                 AR 15 is the civilian version of the M16A, firing a similar round and is considered a "sports rifle"
                 <br/>
                 <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AR-15">
                  http://en.wikipedia.org/...
                 </a>
                 <br/>
                 I personally question its use for home defense or for hunting but that is my personal bias on the issue. Here is another POV
                 <br/>
                 <a href="http://www.longrangehunting.com/articles/semiautomatic-ar-15-rifle-1.php">
                  http://www.longrangehunting.com/...
                 </a>
                 <br/>
                 I would argue it is more of a rifle range type weapon for the sporting shooter
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="cf">
                <p class="sig">
                </p>
                <p class="cb">
                 by
                 <a href="/user/uid:18578">
                  entlord
                 </a>
                 on
                 <a href="/comments/1180214/49121168#c95">

             <ul class="cm i1" id="k49121168">
              <li id="c123">
               <div class="cx" id="cx49121395">
                <h5>
                 <a class="de">
                 </a>
                 <span class="cu">
                  I _think_ we're both right
                 </span>
                 <span class="crd ntb">
                  (
                  <a href="/comments/1180214/49121395#c123?mode=alone;showrate=1#c123">
                   1+ / 0-
                  </a>
                  )
                 </span>
                </h5>
                <div class="crs">
                 <dl>
                  <dt>
                   Recommended by:
                  </dt>
                  <dd>
                   <a href="/user/uid:18578">
                    entlord
                   </a>
                  </dd>
                 </dl>
                </div>
                <div class="ct">
                 <p>
                  I know that the AR-15 is routinely described as a civilian version of an M16. But I think that the AR-15 came first, and was intended for military use (which is not to say "as a high-speed killing machine"). As I understand it, the designers didn't think they were creating a sports rifle.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  I realize that the distinction between "military" and "sports" may be politically loaded, and that really wasn't my intention here. Rather the opposite. It bothers many people when some guns are categorized as "assault weapons"; it bothers many people when some guns are categorized as "sports" weapons; it certainly bothers me when someone says that a kind of weapon is "only to kill children." Perhaps more nuance all around would not be amiss.
                 </p>
                </div>
                <div class="cf">
                 <p class="sig">
                  Election protection:
                  <a href="http://bit.ly/MBYLUn" rel="nofollow">

                   I do consider myself a careful researcher and something of a pedant, perhaps to my detriment.                   </p>

                   That is one reason I ask so many questions. I may be a bit slow or even willfully obdurate, but I try to understand any issue I comment upon as fully as it is within my power to understand

             <li id="c84">
              <div class="cx" id="cx49121114">
               <h5>
                <a class="de">
                </a>
                <span class="cu">
                 I don't do diaries
                </span>
                <span class="crd ntb">
                 (
                 <a href="/comments/1180214/49121114#c84?mode=alone;showrate=1#c84">
                  8+ / 0-
                 </a>
                 )
                </span>
               </h5>
               <div class="crs">
                <dl>
                 <dt>
                  Recommended by:
                 </dt>
                 <dd>
                  <a href="/user/uid:49657">
                   HudsonValleyMark
                  </a>
                  ,
                  <a href="/user/uid:19580">

                  <a href="/user/uid:426">

                  ,
                  <a href="/user/uid:324630">
                   SanFernandoValleyMom
                  </a>
                 </dd>
                </dl>
               </div>
               <div class="ct">
                <p>
                 My mind is swiss cheese and admittedly is failing, almost by the day. I continue to notice new deficits each day. Because of this I feel more comfortable making comments as they don't require the intellectual vigor a diary would. I don't diary because I don't think my attempts would be cogent enough for public consumption.
                </p>
                <p>
                 For the record I detest Yeager, Nugent the NRA and their ilk as damaging the gun owner side far more than any gun control argument.
                </p>
                <p>
                 I am also afraid I do tend to define events in terms of VN because that was one defining moment in my life and presents a frame and context for me to understand events that are happening today. perhaps I do so too often
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="cf">
                <p class="sig">
                </p>

               </a>
               <span class="cu">
                Anyone who is granted or takes for himself
               </span>
               <span class="crd ntb">
                (
                <a href="/comments/1180214/49122819#c176?mode=alone;showrate=1#c176">
                 1+ / 0-
                </a>
                )
               </span>
              </h5>
              <div class="crs">

                 <a href="/user/uid:18578">

              </div>
              <div class="ct">
               <p>
                a sense of entitlement that protects him from being responsible for the consequences of his own actions is in dire need of a reality check. The problem is that the unreality these people live in includes their being - or at least feeling - entitled. When a reality is fostered and held together by those around them who enjoy advantages (money, prestige) from the continuation of that unreality, the sense of entitlement is exaggerated.
               </p>
               <p>
                I have worked with "stars" from various genres over the years - athletics, music, film - and it is sad and disturbing to see what happens to these people when they are brought back to dealing with the real world. It can be, and usually is, a long fall and a hard landing.
               </p>

        <li id="c14">
         <div class="cx" id="cx49120903">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            RE: vaccinating health workers
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1180214/49120903#c14?mode=alone;showrate=1#c14">
             5+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:158085">
              commonmass
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:426">
              Greg Dworkin
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:38543">
              Diana in NoVa
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:117111">
              skohayes
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:89750">
              drmah
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            I would also advocate something that should have been mandatory some time ago. Universal precautions are simply common sense measures to reduce cross contamination. Handwashing is the most simple but the one most ignored. For example, how many healthworkers wash their hands or re-glove between pts or depend 100% on their gloves to prevent contamination (it is possible to contaminate a new set of gloves in the process of switching gloves)? I believe most health workers do not wash their hands an adequate number of times.
           </p>
           <p>
            Talking to a restaurant consultant, he told me he recommended all food workers wash their hands every 15 minutes and every 30 minutes at a minimum, regardless of what they have been doing. He also advocated a protocol with timers so entire crews would wash their hands in concert or in sequence using either a team timer or individual timers.
           </p>
           <p>
            It has been some time since I have been involved in healthcare but it seems to me I know of no local hospital with protocols as rigid as local restaurants (I am not counting the 4 shelves of protocols hospitals have to pass JCAHO accreditation which no one ever reads)
           </p>
          </div>

              Overall compliance improved from 476% in 1994, to
              <br/>
              662% in December 1997 (p&lt;0001; figure 1). Although
              <br/>
              compliance achieved through standard handwashing
              <br/>
              remained stable at around 30%, that associated with hand
              <br/>
              disinfection substantially increased from 136% to 370%
              <br/>
              (p&lt;0001) between the first and the last survey (figure 1). In
              <br/>
              support of this observation, the annual amount of alcoholbased handrub solution used increased from 35 L per 1000
              <br/>
              patient-days in 1993, to 41 L in 1994, 69 L in 1995, 95 L
              <br/>
              in 1996; 109 L in 1997, and 154 L 1998 (p for linear
              <br/>
              trend, p&lt;0001). Compared with the first observation
              <br/>
              period, odds ratios for compliance increased progressively
              <br/>
              even after adjustment for factors independently associated
              <br/>
              with non-compliance (table 2).
             </blockquote>

           <div class="ct">
            <blockquote>
             A new Institute of Medicine (IOM) consensus report supports the safety of the recommended immunization schedule for children from birth to age 6 years in the United States, citing evidence to dispel concerns that up to 24 immunizations by 2 years of age represents too many vaccinations too soon.
             <p>
              "Upon reviewing stakeholder concerns and scientific literature regarding the entire childhood immunization schedule, the IOM committee finds no evidence that the schedule is unsafe," the 14 expert authors write in a brief that accompanied the full report, "Childhood Immunization Schedule and Safety: Stakeholder Concerns, Scientific Evidence, and Future Studies," published online January 16, 2013.
             </p>
            </blockquote>

            </span>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             side effects. I used to get the 'flu shot faithfully every year--I had the 'flu a couple of times before that and hated the experience. In 2007 after I had a reaction to the 'flu shot my doctor forbade me from getting it ever again. I even asked him last year if I could go ahead and get it, but he advised me not to.
            </p>
            <p>
             As for washing hands--yesterday I saw a doctor for the skin problem on my left hand and she advised me to keep my hands OUT of water! This advice is not going to work for me as I am the family cook who washes my hands several times before, during, and after food preparation. I also wash them during the day for the usual reason. At the gym I use hand sanitizer and wipe the handles of the equipment with a sanitizing wipe before I use it.
            </p>
            <p>
             I'll just have to hope I don't get it. The people closest to me have been vaccinated. For all I know, I may have been exposed yesterday at the doctor's office. I was surrounded by coughing, sneezing people.
             <br/>

             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">

              <a href="/comments/1180214/49121065#c67?mode=alone;showrate=1#c67">
               7+ / 0-

            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              and because the strain they vaccinate against changes as the dominant strain changes, you never really know, so there is always a risk.
             </p>
             <p>
              My partner has been in the ER twice this week because he has the flu (and also is severely anemic as a result of some medications he's been taking). As his caregiver, a flu shot is a risk I'm willing to take. NOTE: the vaccine takes about two weeks to be effective, or as effective as it's going to be.
             </p>
             <p>
              The truth is that it's a crapshoot. On the other hand, the flu can kill you.

           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">

            <a href="/comments/1180214/49120975#c37?mode=alone;showrate=1#c37">

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            The NRA is essentially a big myth in several ways:
           </p>
           <p>
            First, it is not an organization comprised of members. (It may have been once.) It is top-down, controlled by money and a small group of manipulators. Much of its membership is free or honorary; folks who subscribe to magazines or take a gun safety course and get a free year.
           </p>
           <p>
            Second, it has far less influence than it claims. See Rachel Maddow's analysis--less effective in influencing elections than even Rove. (Of course, the people they want to influence are already lean-GOP anyway, so there would never be any way to sort that out.)
           </p>
           <p>
            Third, it doesn't represent the membership at all. It's obvious from the idiots that have purported to represent them on television in the past week that they never listen to anyone but themselves.
           </p>
           <p>
            There are new groups forming to try to bleed off membership in ways they might notice, for example the "National Responsible Gun Owners Association" on Facebook. It would be great of a few hundred thousand of those "honorary" members sent them mail saying they want their names removed from the NRA roles.
           </p>
           <p>
            But the NRA will probably never admit they lost any membership, because the "membership" is just a magic curtain to hide the manipulating money men behind.

            <blockquote>
             NRA: NY's quick gun law passage nixed opposition
             <p>
              ALBANY, N.Y. -- The National Rifle Association said the secretive negotiations and lightning-fast passage of New York's tough new gun control laws squelched the powerful gun lobby's ability to mount opposition.
             </p>
             <p>
              Gov. Andrew Cuomo said he had to engineer quick enactment to prevent a counterproductive buying spree of now-outlawed guns.
             </p>
             <p>
              The legislation was negotiated over the weekend, introduced on the first day of the 2013 legislative session and signed into law the next day.
             </p>
             <p>
              The NRA, which has thwarted such restrictions nationwide, had members working the phones but didn't have enough time to coordinate a public rally. The gun-rights group and some New York lawmakers say the rushed legislation also undermined public input and meaningful debate.
             </p>
            </blockquote>

          <li id="c148">
           <div class="cx" id="cx49121683">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              Agreed.
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1180214/49121683#c148?mode=alone;showrate=1#c148">
               1+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:426">
                Greg Dworkin
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              And, so long as rational minds prevail, the worst and most abusive ideas will fall by the wayside.
             </p>
             <p>
              My own bias -- given the fact that most shooting homicides are not mass shootings, and that about 97-98% (I can't remember the number and don't have the study at my finger tips) are not carried out with assault-style weapons, I welcome ANY overture into the realm of "Why are people obtaining and using these stupid guns to kill each other?"
             </p>
             <p>
              Hell -- maybe a few more people will finally get the idea that national security and personal safety will actually be enhanced if more kids can actually grow up with the bare minimum requirements to prepare them for usefual, productive, happy and free lives.
             </p>
             <p>
              And yes, I know I sound like a Democrat when I say that.
              <br/>
              Difference is, I mean it.
             </p>

           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            I'm sick
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1180214/49121355#c119?mode=alone;showrate=1#c119">
             2+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:96394">
              flumptytail
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:166027">
              cordgrass
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            of people saying that opposition to flu shots is irrational. While I'm not opposed to others getting flu shots if they want, I've gotten a flu shot 3 times in my life, in the 90s, and got the flu every one of those 3 years. I haven't gotten a single flu shot in the 21st Century, and haven't gotten the flu once. I don't even think I've had more than one cold this century.
           </p>
           <p>
            I'm very careful about hygiene, especially in public places. I eat in a way that keeps my immune system in good shape. And I know other people with my experience. They got the flu shot and got the flu.
           </p>
           <p>
            I'm not saying the most vulnerable people, especially those with weakened immune systems should not get the shot. And I'm not saying the flu shot causes the flu. The times I got the flu, I think the vaccine didn't match the strains as well as they might in other years. That happens (see CDC website). I was also in poorer health back then.
           </p>
           <p>
            I'm just saying I'm sick of people saying those of us who choose to not get vaccinated are being irrational.
           </p>

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
